<date>1579974979375<//date><Rate>5</Rate><Review>A 10 acre park that has sports a gazebo and historic building. Basketball court, tennis court, horseshoe pit and children's playground.There is an old home, what looks like a servants quarters and a Neff barn. The barn is able to be rented, plus has a lot of historical memorabilia. Historic Neff Estate is open for tours on the third Saturday of every month from 2-4 pm. The tours are provided by the La Mirada Historical Preservation Advisory Council. All tours are free, however donations to aid the restoration efforts are welcome.</Review>< Pics>

<user_name>Cruz Borrero</user_name><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPNXxNNPVzRVZsum1Zl2ybKY7el554vajeNuzsJ=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipM0msu9jW1SsBcQ6a0EG7JxwXgUw7aBkXqUplQ9=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMwooUfTRDCVZaBTD8Td64M59S-E28-FPMgecJm=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOjN3Q6_2ow4Wtymzxk5oVgph0NXlb0USIs1IOp=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics>< Text>
I spent a lot of time researching window replacement companies.  We settled on Hometime Windows and Doors after careful review of four companies and their quotes.

From the quote to the installation, we found Hometime to be professional, considerate, courteous, accommodating, and responsive.

Of the four companies that came to measure our windows and sliding door, Brian from Hometime did the most extensive examination of the existing windows and took the most accurate measurements (I personally observed all measurements and had some concerns about the accuracy of measurements taken by the other companies).

On the day of the installation, Israel and Nate arrived a bit earlier than scheduled.  They arrived wearing masks in consideration of the COVID pandemic concerns and introduced themselves to us.  They walked throughout the house, and around the exterior of the house, to examine the exiting windows and sliding door to confirm the order before starting the removal of the existing windows and sliding door.

Earlier, I mentioned that they were accommodating.  We have a large dog that needed a place to be kept while the work was on going throughout the house.  I asked Israel if they could replace the garage window first so that we could keep the dog there while work was being performed around the rest of the house.  Israel was very accommodating and replaced the garage window first, including the inside trim.

In all, we had 17 windows to be replaced and we were quite impressed with the speed and care in which Israel and Nate performed the work, including the replacement of a large, severely termite damaged, window and supporting vertical wood structures, and the kitchen‚Äôs corner windows.  All the work, except for the sliding door, was completed in one day with the help of a third crew member that join Israel and Nate mid-morning.  I have been in construction most of my adult life and was certain that it would require two full days to replace all the windows, but I was pleasantly wrong.  The sliding door replacement was completed on the following day.

All the work, including cleanup and haul away of the old windows and sliding door, was completed in the 2 days scheduled.  We are very satisfied with Hometime Windows and Doors‚Äô performance, their products, and the finished work, and would absolutely recommend them to families, friends, and neighbors.

The following photos are just 2 of the 17 windows replaced.  In my opinion, these were the most difficult windows to replace.  All that's left is to clean, sand and paint the sill.</Text>

< Text>
This place has its act together.  No wait staff robots here.  Exhibition cooking exposing the full kitchen with seating all around.  It's a joy to watch this group in action.

We were right opposite the handmade pizza production. Station 1, sprinkling the paddles with coarsely ground corn, air stretching the road-dimple-sized dough portions to fit the paddle, ladeling a 1 inch wide thin layer of olive oil around the outer region 1" from the edge; then station 2 starting from the inside edge of the olive oil ladeling their tomato sauce to look like the Target logo. Soft Mozzarella cheese chunks are then dropped to for the sauce circles.  Off to station 3 for toppings and then into the oven.  Beautiful to watch the artistry and obvious caring and dedication.

This routine never let up during our 45 minutes.  Yes we had a pizza, mushrooms and fresh arugala.   You will enjoy anything you order.< /Text>

< Text>
I would add this place to the list of my favorite Italian restaurants in LA! Cozy and pretty. Service was outstanding and excellent - I felt really welcomed by the staff when I was there.

Their lunch menu was simple but sincere. We had their Tagliarini and Margherita. The noodles were special and we loved them. Sitting at the bar, we saw the whole process of making and baking the pizza, which was then served directly from the kitchen to our table, and the pizza was just of the kind that would bring one joy.

In addition to all the afore-mentioned, their passionfruit meringue tart stunned me. A symphony of the cloud-like meringue topping, the sour curd, and the crispy buttery pastry - it was more delicious than impressive looking!</Text>

< Review>
Don't wear your Yeezy's here! Unfortunately my first impression left me with a bad taste in my mouth. The waiting area for a table is quite narrow, it's also the walkway in and out of the restaurant. Low and behold, a 400lb dude stepped on my foot, and it actually hurt, a lot. So ladies, be careful if you're in heels.

Regarding the food, it was actually really good, but you have to order correctly. The garlic knot was really good, but if you let it sit for more than 5 minutes, the bread really soaks up the half-cup of oil that the bread is just sitting in, and caution for the string, it's obviously there and not edible, but it somehow ended up in my mouth. I would recommend the garlic knot.

The mixed mushroom pizza was amazing, so was the pasta and the chicken meatballs, as well as the pound cake dessert.

Staff was amazing, employees were super friendly towards each other, friendly to us, and very helpful in describing what each dish consisted of.

In conclusion, watch out for people stepping on your feet, and order cautiously.<//Review>

<user_name>Krish Bhutwala< /user_name><Date>1542350790885< /Date><rate>4</rate><Review>We started with the white bean and market vegetable skillet - a medley of smashed and whole white beans with (at least this time) cauliflower, cherry tomatoes, feta and herbs. It was slightly on the saltier side and could have been  balanced with a touch more acid, despite having a vinegar butter in it. A great starter nonetheless!

The pizzas were fantastic. That 48 hour crust is nicely crisp on the outside but tears apart easily to reveal a chewy, tasty interior. It's nice to find a neapolitan pizza shop whose meat pizzas aren't exclusively beef- and/or pork-based (though I don't doubt these are also delectable options). Vegetarians also have different a number of pizza options to choose from!

The organic chicken meatball pizza was very good. The bottom of the bottom was finished and crunchy enough to stand up to the heavy toppings. I appreciated that there was more tomato sauce than is usually seen (and arrabiata at that). That being said, we also got the 4-cheese and egg pizza, a white pizza that proved to be a good choice.

Bonus: Their pastries are likely on rotation, but I was able to snag the cheddar apple tarte tatin, a superb soft pastry with a salty-sweet caramelized apple topping. 10/10 would recommend. <user>104745565929433688409</user><review>This place has its act together.  No wait staff robots here.  Exhibition cooking exposing the full kitchen with seating all around.  It's a joy to watch this group in action.

We were right opposite the handmade pizza production. Station 1, sprinkling the paddles with coarsely ground corn, air stretching the road-dimple-sized dough portions to fit the paddle, ladeling a 1 inch wide thin layer of olive oil around the outer region 1" from the edge; then station 2 starting from the inside edge of the olive oil ladeling their tomato sauce to look like the Target logo. Soft Mozzarella cheese chunks are then dropped to for the sauce circles.  Off to station 3 for toppings and then into the oven.  Beautiful to watch the artistry and obvious caring and dedication.

This routine never let up during our 45 minutes.  Yes we had a pizza, mushrooms and fresh arugala.   You will enjoy anything you order.<//review>< Name>

<Review>Ordered the pork belly sausage and kale pizza. We asked our server to have the kale removed, so it was just a pork belly sausage pizza. It was delicious. The tomato sauce was creamy delicious and the sausage was also very tasty. It was a very thin 12" pizza that required folding lengthwise to eat without flopping over. Nothing wrong with that, just trying to give an accurate description. The crust was crunchy and gooey; almost Neapolitan. One pizza should be enough to for an average couple. We also ordered the steak salad...also, delicious. The beef was a bit livery, but tasty. The avocado, tomatoes, and mixed greens were flavorful and had a tasty vinaigrette. The wait staff was helpful and friendly and would acknowledged if they didn't know the answer to something and would get an answer right away. The restaurant is a bit loud and a bit cramped, but it's to be expected for this type of restaurant. We went on a Thursday at about 2pm and it was full, but a couple tables were available. With a glass of wine the total was about $64. I would recommend this place for a casual meal for 1-2 people. They probably can accommodate more people, but given the size and popularity, larger parties should probably call ahead.<//Review><pictures>None< /pictures>< resp>

<userid>117148845077078214870</userid><name>Jason Mckenzie< /name>< date>
1560194591124< /date>
<rate>4</rate>< Review>
Don't wear your Yeezy's here! Unfortunately my first impression left me with a bad taste in my mouth. The waiting area for a table is quite narrow, it's also the walkway in and out of the restaurant. Low and behold, a 400lb dude stepped on my foot, and it actually hurt, a lot. So ladies, be careful if you're in heels.

Regarding the food, it was actually really good, but you have to order correctly. The garlic knot was really good, but if you let it sit for more than 5 minutes, the bread really soaks up the half-cup of oil that the bread is just sitting in, and caution for the string, it's obviously there and not edible, but it somehow ended up in my mouth. I would recommend the garlic knot.

The mixed mushroom pizza was amazing, so was the pasta and the chicken meatballs, as well as the pound cake dessert.

Staff was amazing, employees were super friendly towards each other, friendly to us, and very helpful in describing what each dish consisted of.

In conclusion, watch out for people stepping on your feet, and order cautiously.</Review>

<user_name>Monica Mimzy Faillace</user_name><review>Came here on a Thursday night and it was already super packed by around 7:30. There was about a 45 minute wait, but we left our name and moved in towards the back of the restaurant where there was some room to stand and ordered a bottle of wine while we waited. They were super attentive to us while we waited, and even let us order our food while we were still standing in order to have it ready once we sat down because we were in a bit of a rush.

Regarding drinks, we did a bottle of wine even though some of us wouldn't have preferred it, because the cocktails were on the expensive side. I'm from NYC, but $15 for a cocktail with dinner was still a lot, considering with 2 of those you're already at a $30 tab each not including food, tax, tip, etc. The wine was luckily great though, so we were fine with it once we tried it.

The ambiance was super upbeat while still being cozy. The place itself is small and while it was a bit loud (it was super crowded), it still had an intimate feel. The staff was all extremely friendly and accommodating - my friend who we were with is vegan and found limited options on the menu, but they answered all her questions and were able to switch a few things around to make some of the menu items vegan for her.

She ended up getting the gnocchi and my friend and I split the margarita pizza. Both were really good, but also pretty pricey for what it was.

We really liked Milo and Olive, but I wouldn't recommend it for a casual dinner - better for something a little more formal or special just cased on the price! Definitely a lot of menu options I would have liked to try, but the pricing in general dissuaded me from adding sides, apps etc.

Also, wanted to note that they let us (and everyone) know that "A 3% charge is added by the restaurant to all checks to help offer fully covered healthcare to our employees." While I think this is awesome, I don't necessarily think that's what customers should be paying for? Not sure how it works in other restaurants, but I know plenty of servers and bartenders that get full benefits without it being added to customers' bills. Maybe it's worked into the prices in other ways, but I can tell you for sure if the prices had been any higher we would have relocated for what was a casual night out!<//review></record></dataset><record>

< review>
A great vibe, perfect for date night or catching up with friends. It took a little while for a party of two to get seated but it was worth the wait.

::Food::
- GARLIC KNOTT!!!! It was amazing and perfect for foodies who likes to take pics. The garlic hit the spot, the bread soaked everything up.
-Arugula Salad: I'm going through a phase where I crave for arugula. This was amazing, I don't mind getting one order and finishing it on my own. The portion was large enough to share between the two of us and get seconds.
- Pork Pizza, wasn't disappointing. I think I was expecting more fattiness, but it was ok.

::Parking:: I found street parking, make sure to read the signs!

:: Service:: I liked how attentive they were even though it was super busy.</review>

<user_name>Shalizeh Djahed<//user_name>< Review>
Is it normal that I think about the food at Milo and Olive on the regular? Yes, its a small restaurant where you will almost always have to wait - but it is worth that wait.

The meatballs - amazing. I wish I could recreate this at home!
The garlic knot - my friends still talk about it
The pizzas! - They offer specials that are imaginative and creative (cauliflower pizza was on point). They also have some favorites that are well executed.
The baked goods are also delicious and available to take home.

Postmates will deliver! Expect to wait, ive been here for both lunch and dinner at "off hours" and we had a glass of wine while waiting for a spot to open up. Again it is worth it!< /Review>
